### Additional notes

A fairly rare case of an empty enum with a single-line comment inside. 

Formatting causes terminating brace on an enum to be a part of the comment. This doesn't seem to be the case for other similar declarations.

     9	use oxc_span::SourceType;
    10	
    11	fn main() {
    12	    let out_dir = env::var("OUT_DIR").unwrap();
    13	    let dest_path = Path::new(&out_dir).join("generated_tests.rs");
    14	    let mut f = File::create(&dest_path).unwrap();
    15	
    16	    let fixtures_dir = Path::new("tests/fixtures");
    17	
    18	    if !fixtures_dir.exists() {
    19	        // If no fixtures directory exists, create an empty file
    20	        writeln!(f, "// No test fixtures found").unwrap();
    21	        return;
    22	    }
    23	
    24	    writeln!(f, "// Auto-generated test modules and functions").unwrap();
    25	    writeln!(f).unwrap();
    26	
    27	    // Collect all test files organized by directory
    28	    let mut dir_structure = DirStructure::new();
    29	    collect_tests(fixtures_dir, fixtures_dir, &mut dir_structure).unwrap();
    30	
    31	    // Generate nested modules
    32	    generate_modules(&mut f, &dir_structure, 0).unwrap();
    33	
    34	    println!("cargo:rerun-if-changed=tests/fixtures");
    35	}
    36	
    37	#[derive(Default)]
    38	struct DirStructure {
    39	    /// Test files in this directory (relative paths from fixtures root)
    40	    test_files: Vec<PathBuf>,
    41	    /// Subdirectories
    42	    subdirs: BTreeMap<String, DirStructure>,
    43	}
    44	
    45	impl DirStructure {
    46	    fn new() -> Self {
    47	        Self::default()
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    /// Returns true if this directory or any subdirectory contains test files.
    51	    fn has_test_files(&self) -> bool {
    52	        !self.test_files.is_empty() || self.subdirs.values().any(Self::has_test_files)
    53	    }
    54	}
    55	
    56	/// Collect all test files and organize them by directory
    57	fn collect_tests(dir: &Path, base_dir: &Path, structure: &mut DirStructure) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    58	    let entries = fs::read_dir(dir)?;
    59	
    60	    for entry in entries {
    61	        let entry = entry?;
    62	        let path = entry.path();
    63	
    64	        if path.is_dir() {
    65	            let dir_name = path.file_name().unwrap().to_string_lossy().to_string();
    66	            let subdir = structure.subdirs.entry(dir_name).or_default();
    67	            collect_tests(&path, base_dir, subdir)?;
    68	        } else if is_test_file(&path) {
    69	            let relative_path = path.strip_prefix(base_dir).unwrap().to_path_buf();
    70	            structure.test_files.push(relative_path);
    71	        }
    72	    }
    73	
    74	    Ok(())
    75	}
    76	
    77	/// Generate nested modules for the directory structure
    78	fn generate_modules(
    79	    f: &mut File,
    80	    structure: &DirStructure,
    81	    indent_level: usize,
    82	) -> std::io::Result<()> {
    83	    let indent = "    ".repeat(indent_level);
    84	
    85	    // Generate test functions for files in this directory
    86	    for test_file in &structure.test_files {
    87	        generate_test_function(f, test_file, indent_level)?;
    88	    }
    89	
    90	    // Generate submodules
    91	    for (dir_name, subdir) in &structure.subdirs {
    92	        let module_name = sanitize_module_name(dir_name);
    93	
    94	        writeln!(f, "{indent}#[cfg(test)]")?;
    95	        writeln!(f, "{indent}mod {module_name} {{")?;
    96	        if subdir.has_test_files() {
    97	            writeln!(f, "{indent}    use super::test_file;")?;
    98	        }
    99	        writeln!(f)?;
   100	
   101	        generate_modules(f, subdir, indent_level + 1)?;
   102	
   103	        writeln!(f, "{indent}}}")?;
   104	        writeln!(f)?;
   105	    }
   106	
   107	    Ok(())
   108	}
   109	
   110	fn is_test_file(path: &Path) -> bool {
   111	    if let Some(ext) = path.extension().and_then(|e| e.to_str()) {
   112	        SourceType::from_extension(ext).is_ok()
   113	    } else {
   114	        false
   115	    }
   116	}
   117	
   118	#[expect(clippy::disallowed_methods)]
   119	fn generate_test_function(
   120	    f: &mut File,
   121	    relative_path: &Path,
   122	    indent_level: usize,
   123	) -> std::io::Result<()> {
   124	    let indent = "    ".repeat(indent_level);
   125	    // Use only the filename for the test name (directories are handled by modules)
   126	    let test_name = file_to_test_name(relative_path.file_name().unwrap().to_str().unwrap());
   127	
   128	    writeln!(f, "{indent}#[test]")?;
   129	    writeln!(f, "{indent}fn {test_name}() {{")?;
   130	    writeln!(
   131	        f,
   132	        "{}    let path = std::path::Path::new(\"tests/fixtures/{}\");",
   133	        indent,
   134	        relative_path.display().to_string().replace(MAIN_SEPARATOR, "/")
   135	    )?;
   136	    writeln!(f, "{indent}    test_file(path);")?;
   137	    writeln!(f, "{indent}}}")?;
   138	    writeln!(f)?;
   139	
   140	    Ok(())
   141	}
   142	
   143	/// Convert filename to a valid Rust test function name
   144	fn file_to_test_name(filename: &str) -> String {
   145	    let mut name = String::new();
   146	
   147	    // Replace non-alphanumeric characters with underscores
   148	    for c in filename.chars() {
   149	        if c.is_alphanumeric() {
   150	            name.push(c.to_ascii_lowercase());
   151	        } else {
   152	            name.push('_');
   153	        }
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    // Remove file extension
   157	    if let Some(pos) = name.rfind('_') {
   158	        let after_underscore = &name[pos + 1..];
   159	        if SourceType::from_extension(after_underscore).is_ok() {
   160	            name.truncate(pos);
   161	        }
   162	    }
   163	
   164	    sanitize_identifier(name, "test")
   165	}
   166	
   167	/// Sanitize directory name to be a valid Rust module name
   168	fn sanitize_module_name(name: &str) -> String {
   169	    let mut result = String::new();
   170	
   171	    for c in name.chars() {
   172	        if c.is_alphanumeric() {
   173	            result.push(c.to_ascii_lowercase());
   174	        } else {
   175	            result.push('_');
   176	        }
   177	    }
   178	
   179	    sanitize_identifier(result, "")
   180	}
   181	
   182	/// Sanitize a string to be a valid Rust identifier
   183	/// - prefix: prefix to add if identifier is empty or starts with digit (e.g., "test" or "")
   184	fn sanitize_identifier(mut name: String, prefix: &str) -> String {
   185	    // Ensure it starts with a letter or underscore
   186	    if name.is_empty() || name.chars().next().unwrap().is_numeric() {
   187	        name = if prefix.is_empty() { format!("_{name}") } else { format!("{prefix}_{name}") };
   188	    }
   189	
   190	    // Handle reserved keywords
   191	    if is_reserved_keyword(&name) {
   192	        return format!("r#{name}");
   193	    }
   194	
   195	    name
   196	}
   197	
   198	/// Check if a string is a Rust reserved keyword
   199	fn is_reserved_keyword(s: &str) -> bool {
   200	    matches!(
   201	        s,
   202	        "mod"
   203	            | "fn"
   204	            | "let"
   205	            | "mut"
   206	            | "const"

    16	#[derive(Clone, Copy)]
    17	pub enum ObjectLike<'a, 'b> {
    18	    ObjectExpression(&'b AstNode<'a, ObjectExpression<'a>>),
    19	    TSTypeLiteral(&'b AstNode<'a, TSTypeLiteral<'a>>),
    20	}
    21	
    22	impl<'a> ObjectLike<'a, '_> {
    23	    fn span(&self) -> Span {
    24	        match self {
    25	            ObjectLike::ObjectExpression(o) => o.span,
    26	            ObjectLike::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.span,
    27	        }
    28	    }
    29	
    30	    fn should_hug(&self, f: &Formatter<'_, 'a>) -> bool {
    31	        // Check if the object type is the type annotation of the only parameter in a function.
    32	        // This prevents breaking object properties in cases like:
    33	        // const fn = ({ foo }: { foo: string }) => { ... };
    34	        matches!(self, Self::TSTypeLiteral(node) if {
    35	            // Check if parent is TSTypeAnnotation
    36	            matches!(node.parent(), AstNodes::TSTypeAnnotation(type_ann) if {
    37	                match &type_ann.parent() {
    38	                    AstNodes::FormalParameter(param) if param.initializer.is_none() => {
    39	                        let AstNodes::FormalParameters(parameters) = &param.parent() else {
    40	                            unreachable!()
    41	                        };
    42	                        let this_param = get_this_param(parameters.parent());
    43	                        should_hug_function_parameters(parameters, this_param, false, f)
    44	
    45	                    }
    46	                    AstNodes::TSThisParameter(param) => {
    47	                        matches!(param.parent(), AstNodes::Function(func) if {
    48	                            should_hug_function_parameters(func.params(), Some(param), false, f)
    49	                        })
    50	                    },
    51	                    _ => false,
    52	                }
    53	            })
    54	        })
    55	    }
    56	
    57	    fn members_have_leading_newline(&self, f: &Formatter<'_, 'a>) -> bool {
    58	        match self {
    59	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => o.as_ref().properties.first().is_some_and(|p| {
    60	                f.source_text().contains_newline_between(o.span.start, p.span().start)
    61	            }),
    62	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.as_ref().members.first().is_some_and(|p| {
    63	                f.source_text().contains_newline_between(o.span().start, p.span().start)
    64	            }),
    65	        }
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    fn members_are_empty(&self) -> bool {
    69	        match self {
    70	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => o.properties().is_empty(),
    71	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.members().is_empty(),
    72	        }
    73	    }
    74	
    75	    /// Check if the object is inside a JSX spread attribute or JSX spread child.
    76	    /// In these contexts, empty objects with comments should use soft line breaks
    77	    /// so they can stay on one line if they fit.
    78	    fn is_inside_jsx_spread(&self) -> bool {
    79	        match self {
    80	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => {
    81	                matches!(o.parent(), AstNodes::JSXSpreadAttribute(_) | AstNodes::JSXSpreadChild(_))
    82	            }
    83	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(_) => false,
    84	        }
    85	    }
    86	
    87	    fn write_members(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
    88	        match self {
    89	            Self::ObjectExpression(o) => o.properties().fmt(f),
    90	            Self::TSTypeLiteral(o) => o.members().fmt(f),
    91	        }
    92	    }
    93	}
    94	
    95	impl<'a> Format<'a> for ObjectLike<'a, '_> {
    96	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
    97	        let members = format_with(|f| self.write_members(f));
    98	
    99	        write!(f, "{");
   100	
   101	        if self.members_are_empty() {
   102	            // In JSX spread attributes/children, use soft indent so the object
   103	            // can stay on one line if it fits (e.g., `<div {...{/* comment */}} />`).
   104	            // In other contexts like variable declarations, use block indent to
   105	            // expand the object (e.g., `var a = {\n  /* comment */\n};`).
   106	            if self.is_inside_jsx_spread() {
   107	                write!(f, format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_soft_block_indent());
   108	            } else {
   109	                write!(f, format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_block_indent());
   110	            }
   111	        } else {
   112	            let should_insert_space_around_brackets = f.options().bracket_spacing.value();
   113	            let should_expand =
   114	                f.options().expand == Expand::Auto && self.members_have_leading_newline(f);
   115	
   116	            // If the object type is the type annotation of the only parameter in a function,
   117	            // try to hug the parameter; we don't create a group and inline the contents here.
   118	            //
   119	            // For example:
   120	            // ```ts
   121	            // const fn = ({ foo }: { foo: string }) => { ... };
   122	            //                      ^ do not break properties here
   123	            // ```
   124	            let should_hug = self.should_hug(f);
   125	
   126	            let inner =
   127	                soft_block_indent_with_maybe_space(&members, should_insert_space_around_brackets);
   128	
   129	            if should_hug {
   130	                write!(f, inner);
   131	            } else {
   132	                write!(f, [group(&inner).should_expand(should_expand)]);
   133	            }
   134	        }
   135	
   136	        write!(f, "}");
   137	    }
   138	}

Now I see the pattern. For `ObjectLike` (which handles `TSTypeLiteral` and `ObjectExpression`), when members are empty, it uses `format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_block_indent()`. But for `TSEnumBody`, it uses:

```rust
group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))
```

This doesn't have any indent mode set (no `.with_block_indent()` or `.with_soft_block_indent()`). The default mode is `None` which just outputs the comments inline, and then `soft_line_break()` adds a space or newline.

     1	//! High-level comment formatting interface for the on-demand comment system.
     2	//!
     3	//! This module provides the formatting implementations that work with the cursor-based
     4	//! comment tracking system in [`crate::formatter::comments`]. It handles the actual
     5	//! rendering of comments with proper spacing, line breaks, and indentation.
     6	//!
     7	//! ## Integration with Comment Architecture
     8	//!
     9	//! This module is the "formatting layer" of our on-demand comment system:
    10	//!
    11	//! 1. **AST formatting code calls** the format functions in this module
    12	//! 2. **These functions query** the comment system for relevant comments
    13	//! 3. **Comments are formatted** with appropriate spacing and breaks
    14	//! 4. **The cursor is advanced** to mark comments as processed
    15	//!
    16	//! ## Comment Formatting Implementation
    17	//!
    18	//! ### Leading Comment Formatting ([`FormatLeadingComments`])
    19	//! ```rust,ignore
    20	//! // In AST node formatting:
    21	//! write!(f, [format_leading_comments(node.span)]);
    22	//! write!(f, [node]);
    23	//! ```
    24	//!
    25	//! **Implementation**:
    26	//! 1. Calls `comments_before(node.span.start)` to get unprinted leading comments
    27	//! 2. Formats each comment with spacing based on line breaks in original source
    28	//! 3. Advances cursor by calling `increment_printed_count()` for each comment
    29	//! 4. Handles special cases like JSDoc comment "nestling"
    30	//!
    31	//! ### Trailing Comment Formatting ([`FormatTrailingComments`])
    32	//! ```rust,ignore
    33	//! // In AST node formatting:
    34	//! write!(f, [node]);
    35	//! write!(f, [format_trailing_comments(enclosing, preceding, following)]);
    36	//! ```
    37	//!
    38	//! **Implementation**:
    39	//! 1. Calls `get_trailing_comments()` with node context to determine ownership
    40	//! 2. Uses line suffixes to prevent comments from interfering with code layout
    41	//! 3. Handles complex spacing rules for different comment types
    42	//! 4. Advances cursor after processing each comment
    43	//!
    44	//! ### Dangling Comment Formatting ([`FormatDanglingComments`])
    45	//! ```rust,ignore
    46	//! // In container node formatting:
    47	//! write!(f, [
    48	//!     "{",
    49	//!     format_dangling_comments(container.span).with_block_indent(),
    50	//!     "}"
    51	//! ]);
    52	//! ```
    53	//!
    54	//! **Implementation**:
    55	//! 1. Calls `comments_between()` to find internal comments not owned by children
    56	//! 2. Applies indentation based on container type (block, soft, none)
    57	//! 3. Preserves comment relationships and spacing
    58	//! 4. Advances cursor for processed comments
    59	use oxc_allocator::StringBuilder;
    60	use oxc_ast::{Comment, CommentContent, CommentKind};
    61	use oxc_span::Span;
    62	use oxc_syntax::line_terminator::LineTerminatorSplitter;
    63	
    64	use crate::{JsLabels, write};
    65	
    66	use super::prelude::*;
    67	
    68	/// Returns true if:
    69	/// - `next_comment` is Some, and
    70	/// - both comments are documentation comments, and
    71	/// - both comments are multiline, and
    72	/// - the two comments are immediately adjacent to each other, with no characters between them.
    73	///
    74	/// In this case, the comments are considered "nestled" - a pattern that JSDoc uses to represent
    75	/// overloaded types, which get merged together to create the final type for the subject. The
    76	/// comments must be kept immediately adjacent after formatting to preserve this behavior.
    77	///
    78	/// There isn't much documentation about this behavior, but it is mentioned on the JSDoc repo
    79	/// for documentation: <https://github.com/jsdoc/jsdoc.github.io/issues/40>. Prettier also
    80	/// implements the same behavior: <https://github.com/prettier/prettier/pull/13445/files#diff-3d5eaa2a1593372823589e6e55e7ca905f7c64203ecada0aa4b3b0cdddd5c3ddR160-R178>
    81	fn should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(current: &Comment, next: &Comment) -> bool {
    82	    matches!(current.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc)
    83	        && matches!(next.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc)
    84	        && current.is_multiline_block()
    85	        && next.is_multiline_block()
    86	        && current.span.end == next.span.start
    87	}
    88	
    89	/// Formats the leading comments of `node`
    90	#[inline]
    91	pub const fn format_leading_comments<'a>(span: Span) -> FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
    92	    FormatLeadingComments::Node(span)
    93	}
    94	
    95	/// Formats the leading comments of a node.
    96	#[derive(Debug, Copy, Clone)]
    97	pub enum FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
    98	    Node(Span),
    99	    Comments(&'a [Comment]),
   100	}
   101	
   102	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatLeadingComments<'a> {
   103	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   104	        fn format_leading_comments_impl<'a>(
   105	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   106	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   107	        ) {
   108	            let mut leading_comments_iter = comments.into_iter().peekable();
   109	            while let Some(comment) = leading_comments_iter.next() {
   110	                f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   111	                write!(f, comment);
   112	
   113	                match comment.kind {
   114	                    CommentKind::SingleLineBlock | CommentKind::MultiLineBlock => {
   115	                        match f.source_text().lines_after(comment.span.end) {
   116	                            0 => {
   117	                                let should_nestle =
   118	                                    leading_comments_iter.peek().is_some_and(|next_comment| {
   119	                                        should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(comment, next_comment)
   120	                                    });
   121	
   122	                                write!(f, [maybe_space(!should_nestle)]);
   123	                            }
   124	                            1 => {
   125	                                if f.source_text().get_lines_before(comment.span, f.comments()) == 0
   126	                                {
   127	                                    write!(f, [soft_line_break_or_space()]);
   128	                                } else {
   129	                                    write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
   130	                                }
   131	                            }
   132	                            _ => write!(f, [empty_line()]),
   133	                        }
   134	                    }
   135	                    CommentKind::Line => match f.source_text().lines_after(comment.span.end) {
   136	                        0 | 1 => write!(f, [hard_line_break()]),
   137	                        _ => write!(f, [empty_line()]),
   138	                    },
   139	                }
   140	            }
   141	        }
   142	
   143	        match self {
   144	            Self::Node(span) => {
   145	                let leading_comments = f.context().comments().comments_before(span.start);
   146	                if leading_comments.is_empty() {
   147	                    return;
   148	                }
   149	                format_leading_comments_impl(leading_comments, f);
   150	            }
   151	            Self::Comments(comments) => {
   152	                if comments.is_empty() {
   153	                    return;
   154	                }
   155	                format_leading_comments_impl(*comments, f);
   156	            }
   157	        }
   158	    }
   159	}
   160	
   161	/// Formats the trailing comments of `node`.
   162	#[inline]
   163	pub const fn format_trailing_comments<'a>(
   164	    enclosing_span: Span,
   165	    preceding_span: Span,
   166	    following_span_start: u32,
   167	) -> FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   168	    FormatTrailingComments::Node((enclosing_span, preceding_span, following_span_start))
   169	}
   170	
   171	/// Formats the trailing comments of `node`
   172	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy)]
   173	pub enum FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   174	    // (enclosing_span, preceding_span, following_span_start)
   175	    Node((Span, Span, u32)),
   176	    Comments(&'a [Comment]),
   177	}
   178	
   179	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatTrailingComments<'a> {
   180	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   181	        fn format_trailing_comments_impl<'a>(
   182	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   183	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   184	        ) {
   185	            let mut total_lines_before = 0;
   186	            let mut previous_comment: Option<&Comment> = None;
   187	
   188	            for comment in comments {
   189	                f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   190	
   191	                let lines_before = f.source_text().get_lines_before(comment.span, f.comments());
   192	                total_lines_before += lines_before;
   193	
   194	                let should_nestle = previous_comment.is_some_and(|previous_comment| {
   195	                    should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(previous_comment, comment)
   196	                });
   197	
   198	                // This allows comments at the end of nested structures:
   199	                // {
   200	                //   x: 1,
   201	                //   y: 2
   202	                //   // A comment
   203	                // }
   204	                // Those kinds of comments are almost always leading comments, but
   205	                // here it doesn't go "outside" the block and turns it into a
   206	                // trailing comment for `2`. We can simulate the above by checking
   207	                // if this a comment on its own line; normal trailing comments are
   208	                // always at the end of another expression.
   209	                if total_lines_before > 0
   210	                    || previous_comment.is_some_and(|comment| comment.is_line())
   211	                {
   212	                    write!(
   213	                        f,
   214	                        [line_suffix(&format_with(|f| {
   215	                            match lines_before {
   216	                                _ if should_nestle => {}
   217	                                0 => {
   218	                                    // If the comment is immediately following a block-like comment,
   219	                                    // then it can stay on the same line with just a space between.
   220	                                    // Otherwise, it gets a hard break.
   221	                                    //
   222	                                    //   [>* hello <] // hi
   223	                                    //   [>*
   224	                                    //    * docs
   225	                                    //   */ [> still on the same line <]
   226	                                    if previous_comment.copied().is_some_and(Comment::is_line) {
   227	                                        write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
   228	                                    } else {
   229	                                        write!(f, [space()]);
   230	                                    }
   231	                                }
   232	                                1 => write!(f, [hard_line_break()]),
   233	                                _ => write!(f, [empty_line()]),
   234	                            }
   235	
   236	                            write!(f, [comment]);
   237	                        }))]
   238	                    );
   239	                } else {
   240	                    let content =
   241	                        format_with(|f| write!(f, [maybe_space(!should_nestle), comment]));
   242	
   243	                    if comment.is_line() {
   244	                        write!(f, [line_suffix(&content), expand_parent()]);
   245	                    } else {
   246	                        write!(f, [content]);
   247	                    }
   248	                }
   249	
   250	                previous_comment = Some(comment);
   251	            }
   252	        }
   253	
   254	        match self {
   255	            Self::Node((enclosing_span, preceding_span, following_span_start)) => {
   256	                let comments = f.context().comments().get_trailing_comments(
   257	                    *enclosing_span,
   258	                    *preceding_span,
   259	                    *following_span_start,
   260	                );
   261	
   262	                if comments.is_empty() {
   263	                    return;
   264	                }
   265	
   266	                format_trailing_comments_impl(comments, f);
   267	            }
   268	            Self::Comments(comments) => {
   269	                if comments.is_empty() {
   270	                    return;
   271	                }
   272	
   273	                format_trailing_comments_impl(*comments, f);
   274	            }
   275	        }
   276	    }
   277	}

   279	/// Formats the dangling comments of `node`.
   280	#[inline]
   281	pub const fn format_dangling_comments<'a>(span: Span) -> FormatDanglingComments<'a> {
   282	    FormatDanglingComments::Node { span, indent: DanglingIndentMode::None }
   283	}
   284	
   285	/// Formats the dangling trivia of `token`.
   286	pub enum FormatDanglingComments<'a> {
   287	    Node { span: Span, indent: DanglingIndentMode },
   288	    Comments { comments: &'a [Comment], indent: DanglingIndentMode },
   289	}
   290	
   291	#[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]
   292	pub enum DanglingIndentMode {
   293	    /// Writes every comment on its own line and indents them with a block indent.
   294	    ///
   295	    /// # Examples
   296	    /// ```ignore
   297	    /// [
   298	    ///     /* comment */
   299	    /// ]
   300	    ///
   301	    /// [
   302	    ///     /* comment */
   303	    ///     /* multiple */
   304	    /// ]
   305	    /// ```
   306	    Block,
   307	
   308	    /// Writes every comment on its own line and indents them with a soft line indent.
   309	    /// Guarantees to write a line break if the last formatted comment is a [line](CommentKind::Line) comment.
   310	    ///
   311	    /// # Examples
   312	    ///
   313	    /// ```ignore
   314	    /// [/* comment */]
   315	    ///
   316	    /// [
   317	    ///     /* comment */
   318	    ///     /* other */
   319	    /// ]
   320	    ///
   321	    /// [
   322	    ///     // line
   323	    /// ]
   324	    /// ```
   325	    Soft,
   326	
   327	    /// Writes every comment on its own line.
   328	    None,
   329	}
   330	
   331	impl FormatDanglingComments<'_> {
   332	    /// Indents the comments with a [block](DanglingIndentMode::Block) indent.
   333	    pub fn with_block_indent(self) -> Self {
   334	        self.with_indent_mode(DanglingIndentMode::Block)
   335	    }
   336	
   337	    /// Indents the comments with a [soft block](DanglingIndentMode::Soft) indent.
   338	    pub fn with_soft_block_indent(self) -> Self {
   339	        self.with_indent_mode(DanglingIndentMode::Soft)
   340	    }
   341	
   342	    fn with_indent_mode(mut self, mode: DanglingIndentMode) -> Self {
   343	        match &mut self {
   344	            FormatDanglingComments::Node { indent, .. }
   345	            | FormatDanglingComments::Comments { indent, .. } => *indent = mode,
   346	        }
   347	        self
   348	    }
   349	}
   350	
   351	impl<'a> Format<'a> for FormatDanglingComments<'a> {
   352	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   353	        fn format_dangling_comments_impl<'a>(
   354	            comments: impl IntoIterator<Item = &'a Comment>,
   355	            indent: DanglingIndentMode,
   356	            f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>,
   357	        ) {
   358	            // Write all comments up to the first skipped token trivia or the token
   359	            let format_dangling_comments = format_once(|f| {
   360	                let mut previous_comment: Option<&Comment> = None;
   361	
   362	                for comment in comments {
   363	                    f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
   364	
   365	                    let should_nestle = previous_comment.is_some_and(|previous_comment| {
   366	                        should_nestle_adjacent_doc_comments(previous_comment, comment)
   367	                    });
   368	
   369	                    write!(
   370	                        f,
   371	                        [
   372	                            (previous_comment.is_some() && !should_nestle)
   373	                                .then_some(hard_line_break()),
   374	                            comment
   375	                        ]
   376	                    );
   377	
   378	                    previous_comment = Some(comment);
   379	                }
   380	
   381	                if matches!(indent, DanglingIndentMode::Soft)
   382	                    && previous_comment.copied().is_some_and(Comment::is_line)
   383	                {
   384	                    write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
   385	                }
   386	            });
   387	
   388	            match indent {
   389	                DanglingIndentMode::Block => {
   390	                    write!(f, [block_indent(&format_dangling_comments)]);
   391	                }
   392	                DanglingIndentMode::Soft => {
   393	                    write!(f, [group(&soft_block_indent(&format_dangling_comments))]);
   394	                }
   395	                DanglingIndentMode::None => {
   396	                    write!(f, [format_dangling_comments]);
   397	                }
   398	            }
   399	        }
   400	
   401	        match self {
   402	            FormatDanglingComments::Node { span, indent } => {
   403	                let dangling_comments = f.context().comments().comments_before(span.end);
   404	                if dangling_comments.is_empty() {
   405	                    return;
   406	                }
   407	                format_dangling_comments_impl(dangling_comments, *indent, f);
   408	            }
   409	            FormatDanglingComments::Comments { comments, indent } => {
   410	                if comments.is_empty() {
   411	                    return;
   412	                }
   413	                format_dangling_comments_impl(*comments, *indent, f);
   414	            }
   415	        }
   416	    }
   417	}

   423	            && !self.is_legal()

impl<'a> FormatWrite<'a> for AstNode<'a, TSEnumBody<'a>> {
    fn write(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
        if self.members().is_empty() {
            write!(
                f,
                group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))
            );
        } else {
            write!(f, block_indent(self.members()));
        }

Combined with `soft_line_break()`, the closing brace gets placed right after the comment.

    67	pub fn is_empty_block(block: &[Statement<'_>]) -> bool {
    68	    block.is_empty() || block.iter().all(|s| matches!(s, Statement::EmptyStatement(_)))
    69	}
    70	
    71	/// Formatting of curly braces for an:
    72	/// * empty block: same line `{}`,
    73	/// * empty block that is the 'bons' or 'alt' of an if statement: two lines `{\n}`
    74	/// * non empty block: put each stmt on its own line: `{\nstmt1;\nstmt2;\n}`
    75	/// * non empty block with comments (trailing comments on {, or leading comments on })
    76	fn is_non_collapsible(parent: &AstNodes<'_>) -> bool {
    77	    match parent {
    78	        AstNodes::FunctionBody(_)
    79	        | AstNodes::ForStatement(_)
    80	        | AstNodes::WhileStatement(_)
    81	        | AstNodes::DoWhileStatement(_)
    82	        | AstNodes::TSModuleDeclaration(_)
    83	        | AstNodes::TSGlobalDeclaration(_) => false,
    84	        AstNodes::CatchClause(catch) => {
    85	            // prettier collapse the catch block when it don't have `finalizer`, insert a new line when it has `finalizer`
    86	            matches!(catch.parent(), AstNodes::TryStatement(try_stmt) if try_stmt.finalizer().is_some())
    87	        }
    88	        _ => true,
    89	    }
    90	}

2026-05-31 10:09:21,797 - INFO - swea-agent-oxc-project__oxc-21163 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I see the pattern. For empty blocks with comments, `block_indent(&format_args!(..., format_dangling_comments(self.span)))` is used (without any indent mode suffix, which means `DanglingIndentMode::None`), but it's wrapped in `block_indent`. So the `block_indent` handles the indentation, and the dangling comments are formatted with `None` mode which just puts them on separate lines.

But for the enum body, the current code uses:
```rust
group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))
```

This doesn't use `block_indent` at all. The `group` wrapping with `soft_line_break()` doesn't give proper indentation.

I reproduced the issue. The enum comment is not properly formatted - the closing brace is attached to the comment. The type and interface with comments are handled correctly.

Now let me understand the fix. The issue is in the `TSEnumBody` formatting when members are empty. Let me look at the current code again:

```rust
impl<'a> FormatWrite<'a> for AstNode<'a, TSEnumBody<'a>> {
    fn write(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
        if self.members().is_empty() {
            write!(
                f,
                group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))
            );
        } else {
            write!(f, block_indent(self.members()));
        }
    }
}
```

The problem is: `format_dangling_comments(self.span())` uses `DanglingIndentMode::None`, which just prints comments each on their own line. The `soft_line_break()` adds a line break when the group breaks. But the issue is that the comment itself doesn't get proper indentation, and the closing brace gets attached to the comment because there's no `hard_line_break` before the closing brace.

Let me look at how block statements handle this (lines 38-53 in block_statement.rs):

```rust
if is_empty_block(&self.body) {
    if has_comment_before_catch_clause
        || f.context().comments().has_comment_before(self.span.end)
    {
        write!(
            f,
            block_indent(&format_args!(
                &formatted_comments_before_catch_clause,
                format_dangling_comments(self.span)
            ))
        );
    } else if is_non_collapsible(self.parent()) {
        write!(f, hard_line_break());
    }
}
```

For empty blocks with comments, it uses `block_indent` wrapping `format_dangling_comments(self.span)` (with `None` indent mode). The `block_indent` handles the indentation of the comments + adds line breaks before and after.

The fix for the enum body should be similar: when members are empty, use `block_indent(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span())))` instead of `group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))`.

But wait, we also need to handle the case where there are NO comments in an empty enum. Currently, with no comments, the `group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))` would just produce a `soft_line_break()` inside the braces, which collapses to nothing (empty line). With `block_indent`, we need to make sure empty enums without comments still work.

Let me check: `format_dangling_comments` with no comments returns early (line 404-406 in trivia.rs), so `block_indent(&format_dangling_comments(...))` would produce nothing. But `block_indent` always adds `indent` and `dedent` with hard line breaks. Let me check:

2026-05-31 10:19:14,943 - INFO - swea-agent-oxc-project__oxc-21163 - 💭 THOUGHT
No existing enum test fixtures. Now let me understand the fix properly and implement it.

Looking at the current code for `TSEnumBody`:

```rust
impl<'a> FormatWrite<'a> for AstNode<'a, TSEnumBody<'a>> {
    fn write(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
        if self.members().is_empty() {
            write!(
                f,
                group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))
            );
        } else {
            write!(f, block_indent(self.members()));
        }
    }
}
```

The issue: When there are dangling comments in an empty enum body, the current code uses `group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))`. This means:
1. `format_dangling_comments(self.span())` with `DanglingIndentMode::None` prints the comment on its own line but without any indentation
2. `soft_line_break()` creates a line break when the group breaks
3. The `group` wrapping makes it so that if it fits on one line, everything stays on one line

The problem is that the line comment `// ...` forces a break (since it's a line comment), but the closing brace gets attached right after the comment because there's no proper indentation and the `soft_line_break()` after the comment doesn't properly separate the comment from the closing brace.

Let me look at what the correct fix should be. Looking at how `block_statement.rs` handles empty blocks with dangling comments:

```rust
write!(
    f,
    block_indent(&format_args!(
        &formatted_comments_before_catch_clause,
        format_dangling_comments(self.span)
    ))
);
```

And how `object_like.rs` handles empty objects with dangling comments:

```rust
if self.is_inside_jsx_spread() {
    write!(f, format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_soft_block_indent());
} else {
    write!(f, format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_block_indent());
}
```

The `with_block_indent()` changes the indent mode to `DanglingIndentMode::Block`, which wraps the comments in `block_indent(...)`. Let me trace what happens:

In trivia.rs line 388-398:
```rust
match indent {
    DanglingIndentMode::Block => {
        write!(f, [block_indent(&format_dangling_comments)]);
    }
    DanglingIndentMode::Soft => {
        write!(f, [group(&soft_block_indent(&format_dangling_comments))]);
    }
    DanglingIndentMode::None => {
        write!(f, [format_dangling_comments]);
    }
}
```

So `.with_block_indent()` would wrap the comments in `block_indent`, which adds hard line breaks and indentation.

But wait, for the enum body, we also need to handle the case where there are NO comments. In that case, `block_indent` with empty content would produce a line break, which would make `enum Baz {\n}` instead of `enum Baz {}`. But actually, looking at how `block_statement` handles this:

```rust
if is_empty_block(&self.body) {
    if has_comment_before_catch_clause
        || f.context().comments().has_comment_before(self.span.end)
    {
        write!(f, block_indent(&format_args!(...)));
    } else if is_non_collapsible(self.parent()) {
        write!(f, hard_line_break());
    }
}
```

It checks if there are comments before formatting with block_indent. If no comments, it either uses `hard_line_break()` (for non-collapsible parents) or nothing (collapsible, which results in `{}`).

So the fix for enum body should be:
1. Check if there are dangling comments (using `has_comment_before(self.span.end)`)
2. If yes, use `block_indent(&format_dangling_comments(self.span()))` 
3. If no, keep the current behavior (but we might need `soft_line_break()` or nothing)

Actually wait, let me reconsider. For `enum Baz {}` (no comments), the current code produces `enum Baz {}` because `group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))` has empty dangling comments and `soft_line_break()` collapses to nothing in flat mode. That's correct.

For `enum Baz { // comment }` (with a line comment), we need `enum Baz {\n  // comment\n}`.

So the fix is to check if there are comments before `self.span.end`, and if so, use `block_indent` with the dangling comments. Otherwise, use the current `group(&soft_line_break())` approach (or just `soft_line_break()`).

But actually, let me think more carefully. The `soft_line_break()` in the current code serves to allow the empty enum to collapse to `{}` when there are no comments. When there are comments, the group breaks and the soft_line_break becomes a newline. But the problem is that the comments themselves don't have proper indentation.

Let me look at what happens with `DanglingIndentMode::None` (the default). From trivia.rs lines 362-386:

```rust
let format_dangling_comments = format_once(|f| {
    let mut previous_comment: Option<&Comment> = None;
    for comment in comments {
        f.context_mut().comments_mut().increment_printed_count();
        let should_nestle = ...;
        write!(
            f,
            [
                (previous_comment.is_some() && !should_nestle)
                    .then_some(hard_line_break()),
                comment
            ]
        );
        previous_comment = Some(comment);
    }
    if matches!(indent, DanglingIndentMode::Soft)
        && previous_comment.copied().is_some_and(Comment::is_line)
    {
        write!(f, [hard_line_break()]);
    }
});
```

So with `None` mode, comments are each on their own line (due to `hard_line_break` before each subsequent comment), but there's no indentation. The closing `}` would be placed right after the last comment.

In the current code, `group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(...), soft_line_break()))`:
- The group wraps the comments and a soft_line_break
- When the group breaks (which happens because there's a line comment), the soft_line_break becomes a newline
- But the comments themselves don't have indentation

So the output is:
```
enum Baz {// Enum comment, this will break after formatting}
```

Wait, that's `{// comment}` on one line. But the PR description shows it on one line. Let me re-check...

From the PR: `enum Baz {// Enum comment, this will break after formatting}` - the closing brace is attached to the comment. 

But actually, looking at the DanglingIndentMode::None more carefully: it writes `hard_line_break` between comments, but what about the first comment? There's no line break before the first comment. So the first comment starts right after `{`.

Then for a line comment (`// ...`), the comment itself includes the newline. So after the comment is written, the cursor is on a new line. Then `soft_line_break()` tries to add a line break but may not add proper indentation.

Hmm, let me think about this differently. The issue is that for line comments (which include a newline), the closing `}` ends up on the same line as the comment, without indentation.

Let me look at how `Comment::fmt` works:

   419	impl<'a> Format<'a> for Comment {
   420	    fn fmt(&self, f: &mut Formatter<'_, 'a>) {
   421	        // JSDoc formatting: if enabled, try to format JSDoc comments
   422	        if self.is_jsdoc()
   423	            && !self.is_legal()
   424	            && let Some(jsdoc_options) = &f.options().jsdoc
   425	        {
   426	            let source: &str = &f.source_text();
   427	            let line_width = f.options().line_width.value() as usize;
   428	            // Calculate indent by counting whitespace immediately before the comment,
   429	            // walking backward and stopping at the first non-whitespace character.
   430	            // This matches upstream prettier-plugin-jsdoc's `getIndentationWidth()`:
   431	            //   for (let i = comment.loc.start.column - 1; i >= 0; i--) {
   432	            //     if (c === " ") spaces++; else if (c === "\t") tabs++; else break;
   433	            //   }
   434	            // For standalone comments (start of line), this equals the full indent.
   435	            // For inline comments (mid-expression, e.g. `? /** @type */`), this only
   436	            // counts the adjacent whitespace, giving more room for the comment content
   437	            // and preventing unnecessary type wrapping.
   438	            let indent_chars = {
   439	                let start = self.span.start as usize;
   440	                let before = &source[..start];
   441	                let tab_width = f.options().indent_width.value() as usize;
   442	                before
   443	                    .bytes()
   444	                    .rev()
   445	                    .take_while(|&b| b == b' ' || b == b'\t')
   446	                    .map(|b| if b == b'\t' { tab_width } else { 1 })
   447	                    .sum::<usize>()
   448	            };
   449	            let available_width = line_width.saturating_sub(indent_chars);
   450	            if let Some(formatted) =
   451	                super::jsdoc::format_jsdoc_comment(self, jsdoc_options, source, available_width, f)
   452	            {
   453	                write!(f, [formatted]);
   454	                return;
   455	            }
   456	        }
   457	
   458	        let content = f.source_text().text_for(&self.span);
   459	        if self.is_multiline_block() {
   460	            let mut lines = LineTerminatorSplitter::new(content);
   461	            if is_alignable_comment(content) {
   462	                // Using `write_element` directly instead of `labelled()`
   463	                // to avoid allocating a `Vec` for `lines` iter
   464	                let sort_imports_enabled = f.options().sort_imports.is_some();
   465	                if sort_imports_enabled {
   466	                    f.write_element(FormatElement::Tag(Tag::StartLabelled(LabelId::of(
   467	                        JsLabels::AlignableBlockComment,
   468	                    ))));
   469	                }
   470	
   471	                // `unwrap` is safe because `content` contains at least one line.
   472	                let first_line = lines.next().unwrap();
   473	                write!(f, [text(first_line.trim_end())]);
   474	
   475	                // Indent the remaining lines by one space so that all `*` are aligned.
   476	                for line in lines {
   477	                    write!(f, [hard_line_break(), " ", text(line.trim())]);
   478	                }
   479	
   480	                if sort_imports_enabled {
   481	                    f.write_element(FormatElement::Tag(Tag::EndLabelled));
   482	                }
   483	            } else {
   484	                // Normalize line endings `\r\n` to `\n`
   485	                let mut string = StringBuilder::with_capacity_in(content.len(), f.allocator());
   486	                // `unwrap` is safe because `content` contains at least one line.
   487	                string.push_str(lines.next().unwrap().trim_end());
   488	
   489	                for str in lines {
   490	                    string.push('\n');
   491	                    string.push_str(str);
   492	                }
   493	                write!(f, [text(string.into_str())]);
   494	            }
   495	        } else {
   496	            write!(f, [text(content.trim_end())]);
   497	        }
   498	    }
   499	}

   164	    /// Create a line or block comment at a given location.
   165	    #[inline]
   166	    pub fn new(start: u32, end: u32, kind: CommentKind) -> Self {
   167	        let span = Span::new(start, end);
   168	        Self {

   170	            attached_to: 0,

   180	        match self.kind {
   181	            CommentKind::Line => Span::new(self.span.start + 2, self.span.end),
   182	            CommentKind::SingleLineBlock | CommentKind::MultiLineBlock => {
   183	                Span::new(self.span.start + 2, self.span.end - 2)
   184	            }
   185	        }
   186	    }

   228	            && self.content != CommentContent::Legal
   229	            && self.content != CommentContent::Jsdoc
   230	            && self.content != CommentContent::JsdocLegal
   231	    }
   232	
   233	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is a JSDoc comment. Implies `is_leading` and `is_block`.
   234	    #[inline]
   235	    pub fn is_jsdoc(self) -> bool {
   236	        matches!(self.content, CommentContent::Jsdoc | CommentContent::JsdocLegal)
   237	            && self.is_leading()
   238	    }
   239	
   240	    /// Legal comments
   241	    ///
   242	    /// A "legal comment" is considered to be any statement-level comment
   243	    /// that contains `@license` or `@preserve` or that starts with `//!` or `/*!`.
   244	    ///
   245	    /// <https://esbuild.github.io/api/#legal-comments>
   246	    #[inline]
   247	    pub fn is_legal(self) -> bool {
   248	        matches!(self.content, CommentContent::Legal | CommentContent::JsdocLegal)
   249	            && self.is_leading()
   250	    }
   251	
   252	    /// Is `/* @__PURE__*/`.
   253	    #[inline]
   254	    pub fn is_pure(self) -> bool {
   255	        self.content == CommentContent::Pure
   256	    }
   257	
   258	    /// Is `/* @__NO_SIDE_EFFECTS__*/`.
   259	    #[inline]
   260	    pub fn is_no_side_effects(self) -> bool {
   261	        self.content == CommentContent::NoSideEffects
   262	    }
   263	
   264	    /// Is webpack magic comment.
   265	    #[inline]
   266	    pub fn is_webpack(self) -> bool {
   267	        self.content == CommentContent::Webpack
   268	    }
   269	
   270	    /// Is vite special comment.
   271	    #[inline]
   272	    pub fn is_vite(self) -> bool {
   273	        self.content == CommentContent::Vite
   274	    }
   275	
   276	    /// Is coverage ignore comment.
   277	    #[inline]
   278	    pub fn is_coverage_ignore(self) -> bool {
   279	        self.content == CommentContent::CoverageIgnore && self.is_leading()
   280	    }
   281	
   282	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is preceded by a newline.
   283	    #[inline]
   284	    pub fn preceded_by_newline(self) -> bool {
   285	        self.newlines.contains(CommentNewlines::Leading)
   286	    }
   287	
   288	    /// Returns `true` if this comment is followed by a newline.
   289	    #[inline]
   290	    pub fn followed_by_newline(self) -> bool {
   291	        self.newlines.contains(CommentNewlines::Trailing)
   292	    }
   293	
   294	    /// Returns `true` if this comment has newlines either before or after it.
   295	    #[inline]
   296	    pub fn has_newlines_around(self) -> bool {
   297	        self.newlines != CommentNewlines::None
   298	    }
   299	
   300	    /// Sets the state of `newlines` to include/exclude a newline before the comment.
   301	    #[inline]
   302	    pub fn set_preceded_by_newline(&mut self, preceded_by_newline: bool) {
   303	        self.newlines.set(CommentNewlines::Leading, preceded_by_newline);
   304	    }

fn is_non_collapsible(parent: &AstNodes<'_>) -> bool {
    match parent {
        AstNodes::FunctionBody(_)
        | AstNodes::ForStatement(_)
        | AstNodes::WhileStatement(_)
        | AstNodes::DoWhileStatement(_)
        | AstNodes::TSModuleDeclaration(_)

        _ => true,

}

   ╰────
```

Hmm, line 9 shows the enum with the `}`. But the error points to line 10. This is confusing. Maybe the parser is having trouble because the `}` is on the same line as a line comment, and the line comment consumes everything until the newline, including the `}`?

Actually, wait. In the broken output `enum Baz {// Enum comment, this will break after formatting}`, the `//` comment goes until the end of the line. The `}` is on the same line, AFTER the `//`. So the `}` is actually part of the comment text! The parser sees:
- `enum Baz {` 
- then `// Enum comment, this will break after formatting}` - this is a line comment that includes the `}`
- then EOF

So the parser can't find the closing `}` because it's commented out! That's the bug - the `}` gets appended to the line comment, making it part of the comment.

So my fix correctly addresses this by ensuring there's a newline before the closing `}` when there are comments, and the comments are properly indented.

Let me verify the fix handles the broken-to-fixed case. The broken case is actually syntactically invalid, so the formatter can't parse it. But the fix ensures that formatting valid input produces valid output that matches Prettier.

I see. `comments_before(pos)` returns all unprinted comments that end before or at `pos`. And `has_comment_before(pos)` checks if any such comments exist.

The `format_dangling_comments(self.span())` in trivia.rs calls `comments_before(span.end)` to get the dangling comments. So `has_comment_before(self.span.end)` correctly checks if there are any dangling comments.

But wait, there's a subtlety: `comments_before` returns ALL unprinted comments before the position, including leading comments of the next node. The `format_dangling_comments` is supposed to get only the comments that are "dangling" - i.e., inside the container but not owned by any child. Since the enum body is empty (no children), all comments inside are dangling.

However, `has_comment_before(self.span.end)` might also return `true` for comments that are actually leading comments of the next statement after the enum. Let me think about this...

Actually, looking at the comment system more carefully: `comments_before(span.end)` returns all unprinted comments that end before or at `span.end`. The span of `TSEnumBody` should end at the closing `}`. So any comment inside the body would have its span end before or at `span.end`. Comments after the `}` would have their span start after `span.end`, so they wouldn't be included.

Now let me verify the simpler approach is correct. The key difference between my current simpler approach and the original code:

**Original:**
```rust
group(&format_args!(format_dangling_comments(self.span()), soft_line_break()))
```

**My fix:**
```rust
format_dangling_comments(self.span()).with_block_indent()
```

The `.with_block_indent()` changes the indent mode from `None` to `Block`. In trivia.rs:
- `DanglingIndentMode::None`: writes comments each on their own line, no indentation
- `DanglingIndentMode::Block`: wraps comments in `block_indent(...)`, which adds hard line breaks and indentation

When there are no comments, both approaches produce nothing (early return in `format_dangling_comments_impl`).

When there are line comments:
- Original: comments on their own lines without indentation, then `soft_line_break()` adds a line break (but the closing brace ends up unindented and on the same line as the comment due to group behavior)
- My fix: comments are wrapped in `block_indent`, which adds proper indentation and line breaks before and after

The simpler approach is actually better because:
1. It's more consistent with how other empty containers handle comments (e.g., `ObjectLike` uses `.with_block_indent()` for non-JSX cases)
2. It's simpler code
3. It doesn't require checking for comments separately

Let me verify that the import for `format_dangling_comments` is available. Looking at the imports in mod.rs:
- Line 55: `prelude::*` which includes `format_dangling_comments`
- Line 60-62: `trivia::{DanglingIndentMode, FormatDanglingComments, FormatLeadingComments, FormatTrailingComments}`

But note: `format_dangling_comments` is imported via `prelude::*`, not directly from `trivia`. That's fine.

Now, I'm confident the fix is correct. Let me just double-check the final state of the edited file:
